## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population size P, which is the fundamental problem of population dynamics. The relationship likely involves density-dependent growth models where growth rate depends on current population size, possibly with time-varying parameters.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth with logarithmic density dependence)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Strong Allee effect simplified: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (cubic dependence on P)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (growth with saturating reproduction minus mortality)
- Von Bertalanffy type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Time-modulated logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal variation in growth)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible asymmetric sigmoid growth)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (logistic growth with constant harvesting)
- Density-dependent mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (quadratic density dependence)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power growth dynamics)
- Time-dependent exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponentially changing growth rate)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Quadratic dependence on P (dP_dt ~ P - P²) → logistic-type density-dependent regulation with carrying capacity
- Cubic dependence on P (dP_dt ~ P³ - P² + P) → Allee effect with both lower and upper population thresholds
- Logarithmic coupling log(P) multiplied by P → Gompertz-type growth with multiplicative logarithmic feedback
- Ratio of polynomials in P (e.g., P/(1+P)) → saturating functional response limiting per-capita reproduction
- Fractional powers of P (P^(2/3) or P^(3/4)) → allometric scaling relating metabolic constraints to population growth
- Negative constant term independent of P → constant-rate harvesting or immigration effects
- Product of two linear factors in P → bistability or multiple equilibria in population dynamics
- Periodic functions of time multiplying growth terms → seasonal or cyclic environmental forcing
- Exponential decay in time multiplying P → deteriorating habitat or resource depletion over time
- Sign-changing polynomial in P → multiple steady states indicating regime shifts in population behavior

Candidate formulas: 50

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and determine if any candidate can match it.

## GT Analysis

The GT is:
```
0.1387*(-1 + P/8.038)*(1 - P/70.018)*P + 0.1387*(1 - P/70.018)*P + 0.1387*P/(1 + exp(-8.038*(-0.5894 + P)))
```

Let me expand the polynomial parts:

**First term:** 0.1387*(-1 + P/8.038)*(1 - P/70.018)*P
= 0.1387*(P/8.038 - 1)*(1 - P/70.018)*P

**Second term:** 0.1387*(1 - P/70.018)*P
= 0.1387*P - 0.1387*P²/70.018

**Third term:** 0.1387*P/(1 + exp(-8.038*(P - 0.5894)))

This is a sigmoid-like term.

Let me expand the first term more carefully:
(P/8.038 - 1)(1 - P/70.018) = P/8.038 - P²/(8.038*70.018) - 1 + P/70.018

So first term = 0.1387*P*(P/8.038 - P²/(8.038*70.018) - 1 + P/70.018)
= 0.1387*(P²/8.038 - P³/(8.038*70.018) - P + P²/70.018)

Combining first + second terms:
- P³ term: -0.1387*P³/(8.038*70.018)
- P² terms: 0.1387*P²/8.038 + 0.1387*P²/70.018 - 0.1387*P²/70.018 = 0.1387*P²/8.038
- P terms: -0.1387*P + 0.1387*P = 0

So polynomial part = -0.1387/(8.038*70.018) * P³ + 0.1387/8.038 * P²

The GT simplifies to:
**GT = a*P³ + b*P² + c*P/(1 + exp(-d*(P - e)))**

where a = -0.1387/(8.038*70.018) ≈ -0.0002465, b = 0.1387/8.038 ≈ 0.01726, d = 8.038, e = 0.5894.

Now I need to check which candidates can produce: P³ term + P² term + sigmoid term in P.

The sigmoid term is `c*P/(1 + exp(-d*(P-e)))`. Note that `1/(1+exp(-x))` can't be expressed as `exp(f(P))` alone.

Looking at candidates with structure `P*c1*(P*c2+1)² + ...`:
P*c1*(P*c2+1)² = c1*P*(P²*c2² + 2*P*c2 + 1) = c1*c2²*P³ + 2*c1*c2*P² + c1*P
